                                  CHAPTER I - DEVELOPMENT
PART A - INTRODUCTION
MSP Real Estate, Inc. is in the process of developing land as part of the City Center development
in New Berlin, Wisconsin. The MSP Real Estate, Inc. development site is generally bounded by
W. National Avenue to the north, Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive to the West, Wilbur Drive to
the south, and Deer Creek Parkway to the east. Previous traffic impact analysis (TIA) reports
have been prepared to estimate traffic impacts of the MSP development area, but recent changes
to the land uses on site require an update of the TIA to address traffic impacts and mitigating
improvements to the surrounding street system.
This TIA report updates previous traffic studies with recent peak hour traffic counts collected in
October 2012, current land use estimations for the MSP Real Estate, Inc. development area, and
the following three access alternatives:
    1. No extension of Deer Creek Parkway to W. National Avenue
    2. Alternative 1 plus Wilbur Drive closure east of Cottonwood Road
    3. Alternative 1 plus Howard Avenue extension to Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive
This TIA update also evaluates the remaining development traffic expected from the City Center
West and potential development traffic from lands surrounding a potential Howard Avenue
extension. The location of the MSP Real Estate, Inc. development area and other potential City
Center developments included in this study are shown on Exhibit 1.1.

PART B - ON-SITE DEVELOPMENT
The MSP Real Estate, Inc. development area includes senior housing and apartment buildings
that are currently under construction along Deer Creek Parkway, a three-story apartment building
proposed between W. National Avenue and Library Lane, plus the potential for retail, office, and
restaurant buildings between the three-story apartment building and Michelle Witmer Memorial
Drive. The land uses proposed and estimated for the MSP Real Estate, Inc. Development site are
detailed below:
        34-units senior apartments & 102-units of apartments (currently under construction) ­ see
        site plan on Exhibit 1.2A. Since this development is currently under construction, traffic
        from this development was evaluated with the year 2012 background traffic conditions.
        76-units of apartments ­ see site plan on Exhibit 1.2B. Since this development is being
        planned for construction in 2012/2013, traffic from this development was evaluated with
        the year 2012 build traffic conditions.
        Other potential commercial developments on lots 1 and 2 ­ see conceptual site drawing
        on Exhibit 1.2C. Since there are currently no plans for development on these lots, traffic
        from lots 1 and 2 were evaluated with the year 2012 total traffic conditions.
            o   Retail ­ 11,360 square feet (Lot 2 - estimated from 1.04-acre site)
            o   Office ­ 10,800 square feet (Lot 1)
            o   Restaurants ­ 14,400 square feet (Lot 1)
            o   Retail ­ 10,800 square feet (Lot 1)
As shown on Exhibit 1.2C, access for the residential developments will be through Library Lane
and Deer Creek Parkway. Access for the commercial developments will be through driveways
to Library Lane and W. National Avenue.

Traffic Analysis & Design, Inc.
MSP City Center Development, New Berlin, WI                                        October 16, 2012

PART C - OFF-SITE LAND USE AND DEVELOPMENT
The off-site developments evaluated in this TIA include the remaining buildout for the City
Center West development and the buildout of vacant lands along the northwest side of a potential
connection between Howard Avenue and Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive. Since no
development plans currently exist for the vacant lands, land use sizes were estimated by applying
a 25 percent floor-area-ratio for the approximate 9.5-acres of developable land. The land use
types were determined by estimating 10 percent restaurant space, 25 percent retail space, and 65
percent office space.
The remaining buildout of the City Center West development plus estimated land use types and
sizes for the vacant lands along the Howard Avenue extension are detailed below:
Remaining Buildout ­ City Center West
   Restaurants ­ 14,000 square feet (west of Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive)
   Retail ­ 14,000 square feet (west of Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive)
   Office ­ 9,350 square feet (southeast of Library Lane & Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive)
Potential Buildout ­ Vacant Land along Possible Howard Avenue Extension
    Restaurants ­ 14,000 square feet
    Retail ­ 25,900 square feet
    Office ­ 67,300 square feet
Since specific buildout time-frames have not yet been identified for these sites, traffic from the
City Center West and the vacant land were evaluated with the year 2012 total traffic conditions.

PART D - STUDY AREA
The study area for the proposed developments includes the following intersections:
        W. National Avenue & S. Moorland Road (traffic signal)
        W. National Avenue & W. Coffee Road/Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive (traffic signal)
        W. National Avenue & S. 147th Street (stop sign)
        Library Lane & Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive (stop sign)

PART E - SITE ACCESSIBILITY
The study area roadways are discussed below:
W. National Avenue (CTH ES) is a five-lane two-way-left-turn-lane (TWLTL) undivided
northeast/southwest major arterial roadway with a posted speed limit of 35 mph within the limits
of the study area. According to the Wisconsin Department of Transportation (WisDOT), the
year 2009 annual average daily traffic (AADT) volumes on W. National Avenue in the vicinity
of the study area were 17,800 vehicles per day (vpd) south of W. Coffee Road and 13,300 vpd
north of W. Coffee Road.
S. Moorland Road (CTH O) is a four-lane divided north/south major arterial roadway. The
WisDOT year 2009 AADT on S. Moorland Road was 40,300 vpd north of W. National Avenue
and 30,600 vpd south of W. National Avenue.
W. Coffee Road is a two-lane undivided east/west roadway with a posted speed limit of 35 mph
within the limits of the study area. The WisDOT year 2009 AADT on W. Coffee Road was
6,300 vpd west of W. National Avenue.
Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive is a two-lane northwest/southeast roadway that begins at the
southeast leg of the W. National Avenue intersection with W. Coffee Road and ends just south of
W. Wilbur Drive. Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive is divided with a raised grass median from
Traffic Analysis & Design, Inc.                                                                      2
MSP City Center Development, New Berlin, WI                                      October 16, 2012

W. National Avenue to about 300 feet south of Library Lane. The speed limit on Michelle
Witmer Memorial Drive is 25 mph.
S. 147th Street is a two-lane undivided north/south residential roadway that crosses W. National
Avenue east of Acredale Road. S. 147th Street connects to W. Wilbur Drive. There is currently
no AADT information available on S. 147th Street.
Library Lane is a two-lane undivided east/west roadway within the City Center development.
Sidewalks are present along Library Lane and on-street parking is allowed west of Michelle
Witmer Memorial Drive. Library Lane connects to the Deer Creek apartment's roadway system.

                                  CHAPTER II - TRAFFIC
PART A - EXISTING TRAFFIC
The existing geometrics and traffic control at the study intersections are shown in Exhibit 2.1.
Traffic Analysis & Design, Inc. collected turning movement counts at the W. National Avenue
intersections with S. Moorland Road, W. Coffee Road/Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive, and
147th Street, as well as the Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive intersection with Library Lane. The
traffic counts were collected on typical weekdays between 7:00-9:00 a.m. and 4:00-6:00 p.m.
during October 2012.
Based on the turning movement counts collected at the study intersections, the weekday morning
peak hour occurs from 7:15 to 8:15 a.m. and the weekday evening peak hour occurs from 4:30-
5:30 p.m. The weekday peak hour turning movement counts at the study intersections are shown
on Exhibit 2.2. All traffic count data collected for this study is located in Appendix A.
The City of New Berlin provided hourly traffic count data collected in September 2010 on Wilbur
Drive between Michelle Whitmer Memorial Drive and 147th Street and speed/count data on Wilbur
Drive east between 147th Street and Cottonwood Drive. These weekday morning and evening peak
hour counts on Wilbur Drive are also shown on Exhibit 2.2.

PART B - TRIP GENERATION
To address any potential future traffic impacts along study area roadways and intersections, it is
necessary to identify the hourly volume of traffic generated by the proposed site and off-site
developments. The expected traffic volumes generated by the developments were based on the
size and type of the proposed land uses, and on trip rates as published in the Institute of
Transportation Engineer's (ITE) Trip Generation Manual, 8th Edition.
MSP Real Estate, Inc. Development Site Trip Generation
Exhibit 2.3 shows the background and build development trip generation for the proposed MSP
City Center developments. The background development includes the senior housing and
apartment buildings currently under construction along Deer Creek Parkway and is expected to
generate 800 daily trips, 55 weekday morning peak hour trips, and 70 weekday evening peak
hour trips. The build development includes the 76-unit apartment building proposed for north of
Library Lane and is expected to generate 510 daily trips, 40 weekday morning peak hour trips
and 45 weekday evening peak hour trips.
Exhibit 2.4 shows the MSP site trip generation for additional buildout north of Library Lane.
The additional MSP developments are expected to generate about 2,900 daily trips. Twenty
percent of these trips are expected to be linked trips between the retail developments throughout
the City Center complex, resulting in an expected 2,320 daily driveway trips to the development
driveways.
About 30 percent of the commercial trips (calculated after linked trip reductions) are expected to
be pass-by trips. A pass-by trip occurs when motorists already on the adjacent roadway system
stop off at a development site before continuing on their intended route. This results in an
expected 670 daily pass-by trips and 1,650 daily new trips to the development area.
During the weekday morning peak hour, the MSP development site is expected to generate an
additional 165 driveway trips (40 pass-by trips and 125 new trips) to the study intersections.
During the weekday evening peak hour, the MSP development site is expected to generate an
additional 200 driveway trips (50 pass-by trips and 150 new trips) to the study intersections.


Traffic Analysis & Design, Inc.                                                                      4
MSP City Center Development, New Berlin, WI                                        October 16, 2012

Remaining Buildout ­ City Center West Trip Generation
Exhibit 2.4 shows the expected development trip generation for the remaining buildout of the
City Center West developments. With 20 percent linked trips and 30 percent pass-by trips
estimated for the retail and restaurant land uses, the remaining buildout of the City Center West
is expected to generate 2,000 daily trips (570 pass-by trips and 1,430 new trips), 160 weekday
morning peak hour trips (40 pass-by trips and 120 new trips), and 175 weekday evening peak
hour trips (40 pass-by trips and 135 new trips).
Potential Buildout ­ Vacant Land along Howard Avenue Extension Trip Generation
Exhibit 2.4 shows the expected development trip generation for the vacant developable land
along the potential Howard Avenue extension to Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive. With 20
percent linked trips, the vacant land is expected to generate 2,010 daily/new trips, 155 weekday
morning peak hour trips, and 205 weekday evening peak hour trips.

PART C - TRIP DISTRIBUTION AND ASSIGNMENT
Trip Distribution
The trip distribution for the proposed developments was determined based on the existing traffic
patterns within the study area, the type of proposed land use and the proximity to neighborhoods.
The expected trip distribution for the proposed developments is shown on Exhibit 2.5 and
summarized as follows:
        15% to and from the west on W. National Avenue
        20% to and from the east on W. National Avenue
        30% to and from the south on S. Moorland Road
        25% to and from the north on S. Moorland Road (via W. Coffee Road)
        10% to and from the west on W. Coffee Road
Traffic Assignment
Traffic generated by the proposed developments was assigned to the adjacent roadway system
based on the above directional distribution to determine additional turning movement traffic at the
study intersections. The background traffic assignment for the MSP Real Estate, Inc. senior
housing and apartment development currently under construction is shown on Exhibit 2.6. The
build traffic assignment for the MSP Real Estate, Inc. 76-unit apartment building proposed for
2012/2012 construction is shown on Exhibit 2.7.
The total traffic site and off-site pass-by traffic assignment is shown on Exhibit 2.8 (no pass-by
traffic was estimated for the residential land uses for the MSP development). To simplify the
documentation of site and off-site development traffic on the TIA exhibits, the total buildout
traffic from the MSP Real Estate, Inc. development, the remaining buildout traffic for the City
Center West development, and the potential traffic from the Howard Avenue extension to
Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive were combined into a single traffic assignment exhibit. Note
that since the vacant land surrounding Howard Avenue is not likely to be developed unless the
Howard Avenue extension is constructed, the additional traffic from this area was only
considered for Access Alternative 3. Access Alternative 3 also includes the rerouting of about
60 percent of the existing traffic on Wilbur Avenue, east of Cottonwood Road to account for the
cut-through trips that would no longer be able to access Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive from
the neighborhood area east of Cottonwood Road.
    1. No extension of Deer Creek Parkway to W. National Avenue ­ Exhibit 2.9A
    2. Alternative 1 plus Wilbur Drive closure east of Cottonwood Road ­ Exhibit 2.9B
    3. Alternative 1 plus Howard Ave. extension to Michelle Witmer Memorial Dr. ­ Exhibit 2.9C

Traffic Analysis & Design, Inc.                                                                       5
MSP City Center Development, New Berlin, WI                                       October 16, 2012




Year 2012 Background Traffic
The year 2012 background traffic was developed by adding the background development traffic
assignment from Exhibit 2.6 to the year 2012 existing peak hour traffic volumes on Exhibit 2.2.
The year 2012 background traffic volumes are shown on Exhibit 2.10.
Year 2012 Build Traffic
The year 2012 build traffic was developed by adding the build development traffic assignment
from Exhibit 2.7 to the year 2012 background traffic volumes on Exhibit 2.10. The year 2012
build traffic volumes are shown on Exhibit 2.11.
Year 2012 Total Traffic
The pass-by and driveway trips for each access scenario were added to the year 2012 build traffic
volumes on Exhibit 2.11 to develop the year 2012 total traffic volumes as shown on Exhibit
2.12A for Access Alternative 1, on Exhibit 2.12B for Access Alternative 2, and Exhibit 2.12C
for Access Alternative 3.

   CHAPTER III - TRAFFIC SAFETY AND OPERATIONAL ANALYSIS
PART A ­ DESCRIPTION OF LEVEL OF SERVICE
The study area intersections were analyzed based on the procedures set forth in the 2000
Highway Capacity Manual (HCM) using the Synchro 7 traffic analysis software program.
Intersection operation is defined by "level of service". Level of Service (LOS) is a quantitative
measure that refers to the overall quality of flow at an intersection ranging from very good,
represented by LOS `A', to very poor, represented by LOS `F'. The City of New Berlin has set
overall LOS C as the acceptable LOS for peak hour operating conditions. Therefore, for the
purpose of this traffic study, LOS C was used to define acceptable peak hour operating
conditions. Descriptions of the various levels of service are as follows:
    LOS A is the highest level of service that can be achieved. Under this condition, intersection
    approaches appear quite open, turning movements are easily made, and nearly all drivers find
    freedom of operation. At signalized intersections, average delays are less than 10 seconds.
    At unsignalized intersections, average delays are less than 10 seconds.
    LOS B represents stable operation. At signalized intersections, average vehicle delays are 10
    to 20 seconds. At unsignalized intersections, average delays are 10 to 15 seconds.
    LOS C still represents stable operation, but periodic backups of a few vehicles may develop
    behind turning vehicles. Most drivers begin to feel restricted, but not objectionably so. At
    signalized intersections, average vehicle delays are 20 to 35 seconds. At unsignalized
    intersections, average delays are 15 to 25 seconds.
    LOS D represents increasing traffic restrictions as the intersection approaches instability.
    Delays to approaching vehicles may be substantial during short peaks within the peak period,
    but periodic clearance of long lines occurs, thus preventing excessive backups. At signalized
    intersections, average vehicle delays are 35 to 55 seconds. At unsignalized intersections,
    average delays are 25 to 35 seconds.
    LOS E represents the capacity of the intersection. At signalized intersections, average
    vehicle delays are 55 to 80 seconds. At unsignalized intersections, average delays are 35 to
    50 seconds.
    LOS F represents jammed conditions where the intersection is over capacity and acceptable
    gaps for unsignalized intersections in the mainline traffic flow are minimal. At signalized
    intersections, average vehicle delays exceed 80 seconds. At unsignalized intersections,
    average delays exceed 50 seconds.

The W. National Avenue intersections with S. Moorland Road, W. Coffee Road/Michelle
Witmer Memorial Drive, and 147th Street are expected to operate with movements at LOS D
during the peak hours. The W. National Avenue intersection with S. Moorland Road is also
expected to operate with an overall LOS D during the peak hours. Mitigating delays at these
intersections to LOS C or better would require additional through lanes and/or turn lanes that
may not be feasible to implement due to costs and available right-of-way. Since LOS D or better
conditions is typically considered acceptable operations at intersections, no mitigating
improvements other than signal optimization are recommended for the year 2012 background
traffic volumes.

As shown in Table 3, the W. National Avenue intersection with S. Moorland Road is expected to
operate at an overall LOS D during the peak hours, but with westbound left-turn movements at
LOS E during the weekday morning and evening peak hours and with eastbound through
movements at LOS E during the weekday evening peak hour. Constructing dual eastbound and
westbound left-turn lanes with protected-only left-turn phasing is expected to result in LOS D or
better conditions for the weekday evening peak hour, but is expected to continue to result in LOS
E conditions during the weekday morning peak hour. Mitigating the LOS E conditions for the
year 2012 total traffic scenario with Access Alternative 1 would require providing additional
capacity to the intersection by widening W. National Avenue or S. Moorland Road. Widening
either roadway would require further study and may not be feasible due to right-of-way and
construction costs. Therefore, these long-term widening improvements for the W. National
Avenue intersection with S. Moorland Road have were not included in this report.
The Library Lane intersection with Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive is expected to operate with
eastbound traffic movements at LOS E during the weekday evening peak hour with the existing
geometrics and year 2012 total traffic volumes for Access Alternative 1. To mitigate these delays
to LOS C or better for all traffic movements during the peak hours, it is recommended to install
stop signs on Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive for all-way stop control.
The year 2012 total traffic capacity analysis for Access Alternative 1 with the recommended all-
way stop control at the Library Lane intersection with Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive is shown
in Table 4.

PART C ­ TRAFFIC QUEUE ANALYSIS
The 95th percentile maximum back of queues for the background, build, and total traffic
scenarios are shown on the following exhibits:
        Year 2012 Background Traffic (existing conditions) ­ Exhibit 3.1
        Year 2012 Build Traffic (existing conditions) ­ Exhibit 3.2
        Year 2012 Total Traffic ­ Access Alternative 1 (improvements) ­ Exhibit 3.3A
        Year 2012 Total Traffic ­ Access Alternative 2 (improvements) ­ Exhibit 3.3B
        Year 2012 Total Traffic ­ Access Alternative 3 (improvements) ­ Exhibit 3.3C
The 95th percentile queue is the maximum back of queue with 95th percentile traffic volumes, so
it represents a worst-case queue condition that could be expected during the peak hour, and is
typically used for designing or evaluating turn bay lengths and queue spillback into upstream
intersections. The 95th percentile queues were obtained from the Synchro traffic model, which
includes traffic that arrives during the queue clearance stage (when the light is green, but
vehicles are just beginning to accelerate through the intersection from a stopped position).
Locations where 95th percentile queues are expected to be exceed by at least 50 feet or more are
typically recommended for turn-lane extensions.
Based on signal optimization and the base traffic analysis with the senior housing and apartments
currently under construction along Deer Creek Parkway, the northbound left-turn queues at the
W. National Avenue intersection with S. Moorland Road is expected to exceed the amount of
available storage by at least 50 feet. If signal timings are optimized at this intersection, the
northbound left-turn bay may need to be extended to avoid having the northbound left-turn
traffic extend into the through lane on S. Moorland Road.

                                                                                           ALTERNATIVE 3: ALTERNATIVE 1 PLUS HOWARD AVENUE EXTENSION
             EXHIBIT DATE: 10-16-12                                                                                              NEW BERLIN, WISCONSIN
MSP City Center Development, New Berlin, WI                                         October 16, 2012

          CHAPTER IV - RECOMMENDATIONS AND CONCLUSION
PART A - RECOMMENDATIONS
The following improvements are recommended to mitigate expected delays and accommodate
background, build, and total traffic buildouts for the City Center development in New Berlin,
Wisconsin. These improvements are also shown on Exhibit 4.1.
Note that with existing geometrics and traffic control, the W. National Avenue intersection with
S. Moreland Road are expected to operate with turning movements at LOS D or better (and
overall LOS D) during the peak hours for the year 2012 background and build traffic scenarios.
With the year 2012 total traffic volumes (alternatives 1, 2, and 3), the intersection is expected to
operate with some movements near capacity and at LOS E (but still with overall LOS D) during
the peak hours. Providing additional capacity to mitigate these delays would require widening
either W. National Avenue or S. Moreland Road. Since widening these roads may not be
feasible due to cost and right-of-way issues, it was considered a long-term improvement
consideration and therefore was not evaluated as a recommended improvement in this report.
2012 Background Traffic
The year 2012 background traffic volumes include existing traffic plus additional traffic
expected from the completion of the senior housing and apartment buildings currently being
constructed along Deer Creek Parkway. The following improvements are recommended to
accommodate the year 2012 background traffic at the study intersections.
        Optimize signal timing at the W. National Avenue intersection with Coffee Road to
        reduce delays and queues for all turning movements.
        Optimize signal timing at the W. National Avenue intersection with S. Moorland Road to
        reduce delays and queues for all turning movements.
        Consider extending the northbound left-turn lane at the W. National Avenue intersection
        with S. Moorland Road to accommodate the expected peak hour traffic queues.
2012 Build Traffic
The year 2012 build traffic volumes include year 2012 background traffic plus additional traffic
expected from the construction of a 76-unit apartment building north of Library Lane. The
recommended improvements for the year 2012 background traffic condition are expected to
sufficiently accommodate the additional traffic for the year 2012 build traffic scenario.
Therefore, no other improvements are recommended.
2012 Total Traffic ­ Access Alternative 1
The year 2012 total traffic volumes for Access Alternative 1 include year 2012 build traffic plus
additional traffic expected from the full buildout of the City Center West development and full
buildout of the MSP development area east of Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive. Access
Alternative 1 considers no access from Deer Creek Parkway to W. National Avenue. The
following improvements are recommended to accommodate the year 2012 total traffic for Access
Alternative 1 at the study intersections. These improvements are in addition to those
recommended for the year 2012 background and build traffic conditions.
        Install stop signs on the northbound and southbound approaches of the Library Lane
        intersection with Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive for all-way stop control.
2012 Total Traffic ­ Access Alternative 2
The year 2012 total traffic volumes for Access Alternative 2 include year 2012 build traffic plus
additional traffic expected from the full buildout of the City Center West development and full

Traffic Analysis & Design, Inc.                                                                   13
MSP City Center Development, New Berlin, WI                                       October 16, 2012

buildout of the MSP development area east of Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive. Access
Alternative 2 considers no access from Deer Creek Parkway to W. National Avenue plus the
closure of Wilbur Drive east of Cottonwood Road. The following improvements are
recommended to accommodate the year 2012 total traffic for Access Alternative 2 at the study
intersections. These improvements are in addition to those recommended for the year 2012
background and build traffic conditions.
        Install stop signs on the northbound and southbound approaches of the Library Lane
        intersection with Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive for all-way stop control.
2012 Total Traffic ­ Access Alternative 3
The year 2012 total traffic volumes for Access Alternative 3 include year 2012 build traffic plus
additional traffic expected from the full buildout of the City Center West development, full
buildout of the MSP development area east of Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive, and full
buildout of the vacant land along the Howard Avenue extension area. Access Alternative 3
considers no access from Deer Creek Parkway to W. National Avenue plus an extension of
Howard Avenue to Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive. The following improvements are
recommended to accommodate the year 2012 total traffic for Access Alternative 3 at the study
intersections. These improvements are in addition to those recommended for the year 2012
background and build traffic conditions.
        Install stop signs on the northbound and southbound approaches of the Library Lane
        intersection with Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive for all-way stop control.
PART B - CONCLUSION
Except where noted above, the recommended improvements are expected to provide efficient
traffic operations at the study intersections through the year 2012 with the additional traffic
expected from the background, build, and total buildouts of the City Center development.
The closure of Wilbur Drive, east of Cottonwood Road is expected to reduce the amount of cut-
through traffic traveling between the neighborhoods near S. Sunnyslope Road and W. National
Avenue. The reduction in cut-through traffic is expected to reduce delays and traffic queues at
the Michelle Witmer Memorial Drive intersections with Coffee Road and Library Lane, but since
the cut-through traffic is relatively low, the delay and queue reduction is also relatively low.
Although the access alternatives are expected to provide or restrict different routes to the City
Center development area, and additional development traffic was considered for Access
Alternative 3 (due to the Howard Avenue extension creating additional development
opportunities), the general differences between each alternative is relatively minor. Based on the
traffic analysis conducted for each scenario, similar delays, LOS, and traffic queues are expected
to occur during the peak hours at each study intersection.
